## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations like Duffing, Van der Pol, or driven oscillators are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically forced with damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum driven: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x¬≥, x‚Åµ) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium ‚Äî expect odd polynomials in x for symmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines stability
- Products of v and even powers of x (e.g., v*x¬≤) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type oscillators
- Periodic functions of t (sin, cos) indicate external driving forces; their frequency determines resonance behavior
- Cubic position terms (x¬≥) with opposite sign to linear term (x) indicate a double-well potential (Duffing bifurcation scenario)
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or monotonically dissipated
- Even powers of x in restoring force (x¬≤) break spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x - omega0**c4*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0892*v¬≥ - 0.7253*v*(1 - x¬≤) - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892*v¬≥ - 0.7253*v + 0.7253*v*x¬≤ - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

So the GT has these terms:
1. `c*v¬≥` (cubic in v)
2. `c*v` (linear in v)
3. `c*v*x¬≤` (v times x¬≤)
4. `c*x` (linear in x)
5. `c*x*exp(-|x|)` (x times exponential of absolute value)

The key challenging term is `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is not a standard polynomial, logarithmic, sinusoidal, or simple exponential term. Let me check which candidates could potentially represent this.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))` explicitly. So I need to check if any combination of available terms could reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Looking at candidates with `exp` terms: candidates 4, 44 have `exp(c*x)`, and candidates 3, 5 have `exp(c*t)`.

`exp(c*x)` cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)` because:
- `exp(-|x|)` is not the same as `exp(cx)` for any constant c (due to the absolute value)
- Even if we ignore the absolute value issue, `x*exp(-|x|)` can't be produced from `c*exp(cx)` alone

Looking at candidates with `log` terms: `log(c*x + 1)` cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Looking at candidates with `x**c` (power terms): These are power-law terms and cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Looking at candidates with `(c + x)**4` or similar polynomial terms: These expand to polynomials in x and cannot match the exponential decay.

Looking at candidates with `sin` terms: These are oscillatory and cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Looking at candidates with `v**c` where c is free: This only affects the v-dependence, not the x-dependence.

The term `x*exp(-|x|)` is an essential non-polynomial, non-logarithmic function of x. No candidate formula contains any mechanism to produce this term. All the x-dependent terms in the candidates are:
- Polynomials in x (x, x¬≤, x‚Å¥, (c+x)^n)
- Powers x^c
- Logarithms log(cx+1)
- Simple exponentials exp(cx)
- Ratios involving x

None of these can reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. The absolute value makes it even more impossible since `exp(-|x|)` is not analytic at x=0, while all candidate terms (except possibly `x^c` with non-integer c, but that has issues at x=0 for negative x) are smooth or have different singularity structures.

Even `exp(c*x)` from candidates 4 and 44 cannot work because:
- For x > 0: `x*exp(-x)` vs `exp(cx)` ‚Äî the former has an x multiplier
- For x < 0: `x*exp(x)` vs `exp(cx)` ‚Äî different behavior on different sides

No combination of the available terms in any candidate can reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` as a function valid for all x.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none of them contain terms that can reproduce the `x*exp(-|x|)` component of the ground truth expression.

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x - omega0**c4*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0892*v¬≥ - 0.7253*v*(1 - x¬≤) - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892*v¬≥ - 0.7253*v + 0.7253*v*x¬≤ - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v¬≥` term
2. `v` term
3. `v*x¬≤` term
4. `x` term
5. `x*exp(-|x|)` term

The key challenge is the `x*exp(-|x|)` term. No simple polynomial, logarithmic, or power-law expression can exactly replicate this for all x (both positive and negative).

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce the `x*exp(-|x|)` term:

**Key observation:** `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function that decays exponentially. It cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials (x^n terms)
- `log(c*x + 1)` (not defined for all x, or wrong shape)
- `exp(c*x)` (exponential growth/decay, not odd with decay)
- `(c + x)^4` (polynomial)
- `sin`, `cos` terms
- `v` or `t` dependent terms
- `x^c` for any fixed c

Let me systematically check each candidate:

For **all candidates**, I need to identify if any term can produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. Let me scan through:

- **Candidates with `log(c*x+1)`**: This is only defined for `c*x > -1` and doesn't match `x*exp(-|x|)` which is defined everywhere and is odd.
- **Candidates with `exp(c*x)`**: `exp(c*x)` is never odd, and `c*exp(c*x)` can't equal `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- **Candidates with `(c+x)^4`**: These are polynomials.
- **Candidates with `x^c` terms**: Power laws can't match `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- **Candidates with `t` dependence**: GT has no `t` dependence, so `t`-terms must be zeroed out, but then they can't contribute the needed term.
- **Candidates with `v^c` or `(c+v)^n`**: These involve `v`, not the right structure.
- **Candidates with `sin`**: Trigonometric functions can't match exponential decay.

Going through every candidate (1-50): None of them contain a term that could produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. The available basis functions in all candidates are combinations of polynomials in x and v, logarithms, exponentials of x (not |x|), power laws, trigonometric functions, and t-dependent terms.

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` is linearly independent from all these basis functions, and it has a non-zero coefficient (-1.4474) in the GT, **no candidate can match**.

Let me verify candidates 24 and 22 which have two `x^c` terms - could `c3*x^c4 + c5*x^c6` approximate `x*exp(-|x|)`? No - power laws are algebraically different from `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. They can't be exactly equal.
